| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Android View Rendering Pipeline

## Your Task

Trace how an Android View is measured, laid out, and drawn. Find the key Java source files in `aosp-mirror/platform_frameworks_base` that implement the rendering pipeline: 1. The file that defines `View.java` under `core/java/android/view/` — specifically the `measure()`, `layout()`, and `draw()` methods. 2. The file that defines `ViewRootImpl.java` — the connection between the window manager and the view hierarchy that schedules traversals. 3. The file that implements `Choreographer.java` — the VSYNC-driven frame scheduling. 4. The file that defines `ThreadedRenderer` or `HardwareRenderer` — the hardware-accelerated rendering bridge to the GPU. 5. The file that implements `DisplayListCanvas` or `RecordingCanvas` — the canvas that records draw operations for GPU replay. Report each file path and key class/method.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/android-frameworks-base--d41da232` (aosp-mirror/platform_frameworks_base)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

114-assistanttext-
I've completed the analysis of the Android View rendering pipeline and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings. Here's what I discovered:

## Key Files Found:

1. **View.java** - Defines measure(), layout(), and draw() methods that form the core of the rendering protocol
2. **ViewRootImpl.java** - The central orchestrator that schedules and coordinates the entire pipeline:
   - `scheduleTraversals()` - schedules rendering via Choreographer
   - `performTraversals()` - main entry point that calls measure, layout, and draw phases
3. **Choreographer.java** - VSYNC-driven frame scheduler that coordinates timing with display refresh
4. **ThreadedRenderer.java** - Hardware-accelerated renderer managing GPU resources on a separate thread
5. **HardwareRenderer.java** - Base class managing native GPU context and display lists
6. **RenderNode.java** - Contains display lists with begin/endRecording methods for GPU commands
7. **RecordingCanvas.java** - Records draw operations for GPU replay instead of immediate rendering
8. **BaseRecordingCanvas.java** - Base class for deferred rendering canvases

## Complete Pipeline Flow:

1. **Scheduling**: ViewRootImpl schedules via Choreographer.postCallback(CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL)
2. **VSYNC Signal**: Choreographer receives VSYNC from SurfaceFlinger
3. **Measure Phase**: performMeasure() → View.measure() recursively
4. **Layout Phase**: performLayout() → View.layout() positioning all views
5. **Draw Phase**: performDraw() → RenderNode.beginRecording() → RecordingCanvas records operations → GPU rendering

The answer includes detailed line numbers, method signatures, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how each component integrates into the rendering pipeline for synchronized 60 FPS GPU-accelerated rendering.

This is used to render a scene built\\n59:  * from {@link RenderNode}'s to an output {@link android.view.Surface}. There can be as many\\n60:  * HardwareRenderer instances as desired.</p>\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <h3>Resources & lifecycle</h3>\\n63:  *\\n64:  * <p>All HardwareRenderer instances share a common render thread. The render thread contains\\n65:  * the GPU context & resources necessary to do GPU-accelerated rendering. As such, the first\\n66:  * HardwareRenderer created comes with the cost of also creating the associated GPU contexts,\\n67:  * however each incremental HardwareRenderer thereafter is fairly cheap. The expected usage\\n68:  * is to have a HardwareRenderer instance for every active {@link Surface}. For example\\n69:  * when an Activity shows a Dialog the system internally will use 2 hardware renderers, both\\n70:  * of which may be drawing at the same time.</p>\\n71:  *\\n72:  * <p>NOTE: Due to the shared, cooperative nature of the render thread it is critical that\\n73:  * any {@link Surface} used must have a prompt, reliable consuming side. The user should no longer\\n103:      * attempt to call syncAndDraw until a new surface has been provided by calling\\n104:      * setSurface.\\n105:      *\\n106:      * <p>Spoiler: the reward is GPU-accelerated drawing, better find that Surface!\\n107:      */\\n108:     public static final int SYNC_LOST_SURFACE_REWARD_IF_FOUND = 1 << 1;\\n109: \\n110:     /**\\n111:      * The hardware renderer has been set to a \\\"stopped\\\" state. If this is returned then the\\n112:      * rendering content has been synced, however a frame was not produced.\\n113:      */\\n114:     public static final int SYNC_CONTEXT_IS_STOPPED = 1 << 2;\\n115: \\n116:     /**\\n117:      * The content was synced but the renderer has declined to produce a frame in this vsync\\n118:      * interval. This can happen if a frame was already drawn in this vsync or if the renderer\\n119:      * is outrunning the frame consumer. The renderer will internally re-schedule itself\\n120:      * to render a frame in the next vsync signal, so the caller does not need to do anything\\n121:      * in response to this signal.\\n122:      */\\n123:     public static final int SYNC_FRAME_DROPPED = 1 << 3;\\n124: \\n125:     /** @hide */\\n126:     @IntDef(value = {\\n127:             SYNC_OK, SYNC_REDRAW_REQUESTED, Each RenderNode\\n43:  * contains both a display list as well as a set of properties that affect the rendering of the\\n44:  * display list. RenderNodes are used internally for all Views by default and are not typically\\n45:  * used directly.</p>\\n46:  *\\n47:  * <p>RenderNodes are used to divide up the rendering content of a complex scene into smaller\\n48:  * pieces that can then be updated individually more cheaply. Updating part of the scene only needs\\n49:  * to update the display list or properties of a small number of RenderNode instead of redrawing\\n50:  * everything from scratch. A RenderNode only needs its display list re-recorded when its content\\n51:  * alone should be changed. RenderNodes can also be transformed without re-recording the display\\n52:  * list through the transform properties.</p>\\n53:  *\\n54:  * <p>A text editor might for instance store each paragraph into its own RenderNode.\\n55:  * Thus when the user inserts or removes characters, only the display list of the\\n56:  * affected paragraph needs to be recorded again.</p>\\n57:  *\\n58:  * <h3>Hardware acceleration</h3>\\n59:  * <p>RenderNodes can be drawn using a {@link RecordingCanvas}. They are not\\n60:  * supported in software. All the commands\\n129:  *          // recorded in createDisplayList() won't be re-issued, only onDraw()\\n130:  *          // will be invoked and will execute very quickly\\n131:  *          mRenderNode.offsetLeftAndRight(x);\\n132:  *          invalidate();\\n133:  *     }</pre>\\n134:  *\\n135:  * <p>A few of the properties may at first appear redundant, such as {@link #setElevation(float)}\\n136:  * and {@link #setTranslationZ(float)}.     "content": "1: /*\n2:  * Copyright (C) 2010 The Android Open Source Project\n3:  *\n4:  * Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5:  * you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6:  * You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7:  *\n8:  *      http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9:  *\n10:  * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11:  * distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12:  * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13:  * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14:  * limitations under the License.\n15:  */\n16: \n17: package android.graphics;\n18: \n19: import android.animation.Animator;\n20: import android.annotation.BytesLong;\n21: import android.annotation.ColorInt;\n22: import android.annotation.FloatRange;\n23: import android.annotation.IntDef;\n24: import android.annotation.NonNull;\n25: import android.annotation.Nullable;\n26: import android.graphics.animation.RenderNodeAnimator;\n27: import android.view.NativeVectorDrawableAnimator;\n28: import android.view.Surface;\n29: import android.view.View;\n30: \n31: import com.android.internal.util.ArrayUtils;\n32: \n33: import dalvik.annotation.optimization.CriticalNative;\n34: \n35: import libcore.util.NativeAllocationRegistry;\n36: \n37: import java.lang.annotation.Retention;\n38: import java.lang.annotation.RetentionPolicy;\n39: import java.lang.ref.WeakReference;\n40: \n41: /**\n42:  * <p>RenderNode is used to build hardware accelerated rendering hierarchies. Each RenderNode\n43:  * contains both a display list as well as a set of properties that affect the rendering of the\n44:  * display list. RenderNodes are used internally for all Views by default and are not typically\n45:  * used directly.</p>\n46:  *\n47:  * <p>RenderNodes are used to divide up the rendering content of a complex scene into smaller\n48:  * pieces that can then be updated individually more cheaply. Updating part of the scene only needs\n49:  * to update the display list or properties of a small number of RenderNode instead of redrawing\n50:  * everything from scratch. A RenderNode only needs its display list re-recorded when its content\n51:  * alone should be changed. RenderNodes can also be transformed without re-recording the display\n52:  * list through the transform properties.</p>\n53:  *\n54:  * <p>A text editor might for instance store each paragraph into its own RenderNode.\n55:  * Thus when the user inserts or removes characters, only the display list of the\n56:  * affected paragraph needs to be recorded again.</p>\n57:  *\n58:  * <h3>Hardware acceleration</h3>\n59:  * <p>RenderNodes can be drawn using a {@link RecordingCanvas}. They are not\n60:  * supported in software. Always make sure that the {@link android.graphics.Canvas}\n61:  * you are using to render a display list is hardware accelerated using\n62:  * {@link android.graphics.Canvas#isHardwareAccelerated()}.</p>\n63:  *\n64:  * <h3>Creating a RenderNode</h3>\n65:  * <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\n66:  *     RenderNode renderNode = new RenderNode(\"myRenderNode\");\n67:  *     renderNode.setPosition(0, 0, 50, 50); // Set the size to 50x50\n68:  *     RecordingCanvas canvas = renderNode.beginRecording();\n69:  *     try {\n70:  *         // Draw with the canvas\n71:  *         canvas.drawRect(...);\n72:  *     } finally {\n73:  *         renderNode.endRecording();\n74:  *     }</pre>\n75:  *\n76:  * <h3>Drawing a RenderNode in a View</h3>\n77:  * <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\n78:  *     protected void onDraw(Canvas canvas) {\n79:  *         if (canvas.isHardwareAccelerated()) {\n80:  *             // Check that the RenderNode has a display list, re-recording it if it does not.\n81:  *             if (!myRenderNode.hasDisplayList()) {\n82:  *                 updateDisplayList(myRenderNode);\n83:  *             }\n84:  *             // Draw the RenderNode into this canvas.\n85:  *             canvas.drawRenderNode(myRenderNode);\n86:  *         }\n87:  *     }</pre>\n88:  *\n89:  * <h3>Releasing resources</h3>\n90:  * <p>This step is not mandatory but recommended if you want to release resources\n91:  * held by a display list as soon as possible. Most significantly any bitmaps it may contain.</p>\n92:  * <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\n93:  *     // Discards the display list content allowing for any held resources to be released.\n94:  *     // After calling this\n95:  *     renderNode.discardDisplayList();</pre>\n96:  *\n97:  *\n98:  * <h3>Properties</h3>\n99:  * <p>In addition, a RenderNode offers several properties, such as\n100:  * {@link #setScaleX(float)} or {@link #setTranslationX(float)}, that can be used to affect all\n101:  * the drawing commands recorded within. For instance, these properties can be used\n102:  * to move around a large number of images without re-issuing all the individual\n103:  * <code>canvas.drawBitmap()</code> calls.</p>\n104:  *\n105:  * <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\n106:  *     private void createDisplayList() {\n107:  *         mRenderNode = new RenderNode(\"MyRenderNode\");\n108:  *         mRenderNode.setPosition(0, 0, width, height);\n109:  *         RecordingCanvas canvas = mRenderNode.beginRecording();\n110:  *         try {\n111:  *             for (Bitmap b : mBitmaps) {\n112:  *                 canvas.drawBitmap(b, 0.0f, 0.0f, null);\n113:  *                 canvas.translate(0.0f, b.getHeight());\n114:  *             }\n115:  *         } finally {\n116:  *             mRenderNode.endRecording();\n117:  *         }\n118:  *     }\n119:  *\n120:  *     protected void onDraw(Canvas canvas) {\n121:  *         if (canvas.isHardwareAccelerated())\n122:  *             canvas.drawRenderNode(mRenderNode);\n123:  *         }\n124:  *     }\n125:  *\n126:  *     private void moveContentBy(int x) {\n127:  *          // This will move all the bitmaps recorded inside the display list\n128:  *          // by x pixels to the right and redraw this view. All the commands\n129:  *          // recorded in createDisplayList() won't be re-issued, only onDraw()\n130:  *          // will be invoked and will execute very quickly\n131:  *          mRenderNode.offsetLeftAndRight(x);\n132:  *          invalidate();\n133:  *     }</pre>\n134:  *\n135:  * <p>A few of the properties may at first appear redundant, such as {@link #setElevation(float)}\n136:  * and {@link #setTranslationZ(float)}. The reason for these duplicates are to allow for a\n137:  * separation between static & transient usages. For example consider a button that raises from 2dp\n138:  * to 8dp when pressed. To achieve that an application may decide to setElevation(2dip), and then\n139:  * on press to animate setTranslationZ to 6dip. Combined this achieves the final desired 8dip\n140:  * value, but the animation need only concern itself with animating the lift from press without\n141:  * needing to know the initial starting value. {@link #setTranslationX(float)} and\n142:  * {@link #setTranslationY(float)} are similarly provided for animation uses despite the functional\n143:  * overlap with {@link #setPosition(Rect)}.\n144:  *\n145:  * <p>The RenderNode's transform matrix is computed at render time as follows:\n146:  * <pre class=\"prettyprint\">\n147:  *     Matrix transform = new Matrix();\n148:  *     transform.setTranslate(renderNode.getTranslationX(), renderNode.getTranslationY());\n149:  *     transform.preRotate(renderNode.getRotationZ(),\n150:  *             renderNode.getPivotX(), renderNode.getPivotY());\n151: ",

\"text\": \"# Android View Rendering Pipeline\\n\\nThe Android View rendering pipeline is a complex orchestration between multiple system components that coordinate to measure, layout, and draw views on the GPU. Here's the complete flow:\\n\\n## 1. View.java (core/java/android/view/View.java)\\nThe foundation of the rendering pipeline. Defines three critical methods:\\n- **measure(int widthMeasureSpec, int heightMeasureSpec)**: Determines view dimensions based on parent constraints\\n- **layout(int l, int t, int r, int b)**: Positions the view and its children at specified coordinates\\n- **draw(Canvas canvas)**: Renders the view content onto a canvas, calling onDraw() and child rendering\\n\\n## 2. ViewRootImpl.java (core/java/android/view/ViewRootImpl.java)\\nThe central orchestrator connecting the window manager to the view hierarchy. Key methods:\\n- **scheduleTraversals()** (line 2948): Schedules the next rendering pass via Choreographer, posting CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL\\n- **performTraversals()** (line 3422): Main traversal method that:\\n  - Calls **performMeasure()** (line 4032): Recursively measures all views in the hierarchy\\n  - Calls **performLayout()** (line 4113): Recursively layouts all views based on measured dimensions\\n  - Calls **performDraw()** (line 5348): Initiates the drawing phase\\n- **doTraversal()** (line 2968): Called by Choreographer when ready to render\\n\\nViewRootImpl also maintains the mAttachInfo.mThreadedRenderer (ThreadedRenderer instance) and coordinates surface management.\\n\\n## 3. Choreographer.java (core/java/android/view/Choreographer.java)\\nThe VSYNC-driven frame scheduler. Key features:\\n- **CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL** (line 261): Callback type for handling layout and draw\\n- **postCallback(int callbackType, Runnable action, Object token)**: Posts callbacks synchronized to VSYNC\\n- Maintains multiple callback queues (CALLBACK_ANIMATION, CALLBACK_INSETS_ANIMATION, CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL, CALLBACK_COMMIT)\\n- Uses DisplayEventReceiver to listen for VSYNC signals from SurfaceFlinger\\n- Each Looper thread has its own Choreographer instance for frame coordination\\n\\n## 4. ThreadedRenderer.java (core/java/android/view/ThreadedRenderer.java)\\nHardware-accelerated renderer extending HardwareRenderer. Responsibilities:\\n- Creates and manages a RenderProxy on a separate render thread\\n- Initializes the rendering context when first surface is provided\\n- Manages EGLContext and EGLSurface for GPU rendering\\n- Proxies draw calls to the native render thread\\n- Defines DrawCallbacks interface for pre/post-draw hooks\\n\\n## 5. HardwareRenderer.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/HardwareRenderer.java)\\nBase class for hardware rendering. Key aspects:\\n- Creates a native RenderNode as mRootNode to hold the display list\\n- Manages lifecycle of GPU resources\\n- Provides syncAndDraw() for synchronization with VSYNC\\n- Supports deferred rendering through display lists\\n\\n## 6. RenderNode.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/RenderNode.java)\\nData structure holding the display list and rendering properties:\\n- **beginRecording()**: Returns a RecordingCanvas to record draw operations\\n- **endRecording()**: Finalizes the display list recording\\n- Stores draw commands as a GPU-executable display list\\n- Contains transformation properties (scale, rotation, translation, etc.)\\n- Can be updated independently without re-recording entire view hierarchy\\n\\n## 7. RecordingCanvas.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/RecordingCanvas.java)\\nSpecialized Canvas that records draw operations for GPU replay:\\n- Extends BaseRecordingCanvas\\n- Uses object pooling to reuse canvas instances (POOL_LIMIT = 25)\\n- Wraps calls to native nCreateDisplayListCanvas()\\n- Obtained via RenderNode.beginRecording()\\n- Valid only until RenderNode.endRecording() is called\\n\\n## 8. BaseRecordingCanvas.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/BaseRecordingCanvas.java)\\nBase class for deferred rendering canvases:\\n- Implements all Canvas draw operations as @FastNative calls\\n- Records commands instead of immediately rendering\\n- Used by both RecordingCanvas and potentially other recording implementations\\n- Avoids immediate GPU submission, batching for efficiency\\n\\n## Complete Rendering Flow:\\n\\n1. **Scheduling**: ViewRootImpl.scheduleTraversals() \u2192 Choreographer.postCallback(CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL)\\n2. **VSYNC Signal**: Choreographer receives VSYNC from DisplayEventReceiver (SurfaceFlinger)\\n3. **Traversal Execution**: Choreographer invokes doTraversal() \u2192 performTraversals()\\n4. **Measurement**: performMeasure() \u2192 View.measure() recursively for entire hierarchy\\n5. **Layout**: performLayout() \u2192 View.layout() recursively positioning all views\\n6. **Drawing**: performDraw() \u2192 initiates GPU rendering:\\n   - For each View: RenderNode.beginRecording() \u2192 RecordingCanvas\\n   - View.draw(RecordingCanvas) records operations\\n   - RenderNode.endRecording() finalizes display list\\n7. **GPU Rendering**: ThreadedRenderer queues display lists to render thread\\n8. **Frame Output**: Display list commands execute on GPU via HardwareRenderer\\n9. **Buffer Swap**: Surface buffer presents to display via SurfaceFlinger\\n\\nThis pipeline ensures smooth 60 FPS rendering synchronized with the display refresh rate through VSYNC timing.\"\n}\n",

\"text\": \"# Android View Rendering Pipeline\\n\\nThe Android View rendering pipeline is a complex orchestration between multiple system components that coordinate to measure, layout, and draw views on the GPU. Here's the complete flow:\\n\\n## 1. View.java (core/java/android/view/View.java)\\nThe foundation of the rendering pipeline. Defines three critical methods:\\n- **measure(int widthMeasureSpec, int heightMeasureSpec)**: Determines view dimensions based on parent constraints\\n- **layout(int l, int t, int r, int b)**: Positions the view and its children at specified coordinates\\n- **draw(Canvas canvas)**: Renders the view content onto a canvas, calling onDraw() and child rendering\\n\\n## 2. ViewRootImpl.java (core/java/android/view/ViewRootImpl.java)\\nThe central orchestrator connecting the window manager to the view hierarchy. Key methods:\\n- **scheduleTraversals()** (line 2948): Schedules the next rendering pass via Choreographer, posting CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL\\n- **performTraversals()** (line 3422): Main traversal method that:\\n  - Calls **performMeasure()** (line 4032): Recursively measures all views in the hierarchy\\n  - Calls **performLayout()** (line 4113): Recursively layouts all views based on measured dimensions\\n  - Calls **performDraw()** (line 5348): Initiates the drawing phase\\n- **doTraversal()** (line 2968): Called by Choreographer when ready to render\\n\\nViewRootImpl also maintains the mAttachInfo.mThreadedRenderer (ThreadedRenderer instance) and coordinates surface management.\\n\\n## 3. Choreographer.java (core/java/android/view/Choreographer.java)\\nThe VSYNC-driven frame scheduler. Key features:\\n- **CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL** (line 261): Callback type for handling layout and draw\\n- **postCallback(int callbackType, Runnable action, Object token)**: Posts callbacks synchronized to VSYNC\\n- Maintains multiple callback queues (CALLBACK_ANIMATION, CALLBACK_INSETS_ANIMATION, CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL, CALLBACK_COMMIT)\\n- Uses DisplayEventReceiver to listen for VSYNC signals from SurfaceFlinger\\n- Each Looper thread has its own Choreographer instance for frame coordination\\n\\n## 4. ThreadedRenderer.java (core/java/android/view/ThreadedRenderer.java)\\nHardware-accelerated renderer extending HardwareRenderer. Responsibilities:\\n- Creates and manages a RenderProxy on a separate render thread\\n- Initializes the rendering context when first surface is provided\\n- Manages EGLContext and EGLSurface for GPU rendering\\n- Proxies draw calls to the native render thread\\n- Defines DrawCallbacks interface for pre/post-draw hooks\\n\\n## 5. HardwareRenderer.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/HardwareRenderer.java)\\nBase class for hardware rendering. Key aspects:\\n- Creates a native RenderNode as mRootNode to hold the display list\\n- Manages lifecycle of GPU resources\\n- Provides syncAndDraw() for synchronization with VSYNC\\n- Supports deferred rendering through display lists\\n\\n## 6. RenderNode.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/RenderNode.java)\\nData structure holding the display list and rendering properties:\\n- **beginRecording()**: Returns a RecordingCanvas to record draw operations\\n- **endRecording()**: Finalizes the display list recording\\n- Stores draw commands as a GPU-executable display list\\n- Contains transformation properties (scale, rotation, translation, etc.)\\n- Can be updated independently without re-recording entire view hierarchy\\n\\n## 7. RecordingCanvas.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/RecordingCanvas.java)\\nSpecialized Canvas that records draw operations for GPU replay:\\n- Extends BaseRecordingCanvas\\n- Uses object pooling to reuse canvas instances (POOL_LIMIT = 25)\\n- Wraps calls to native nCreateDisplayListCanvas()\\n- Obtained via RenderNode.beginRecording()\\n- Valid only until RenderNode.endRecording() is called\\n\\n## 8. BaseRecordingCanvas.java (graphics/java/android/graphics/BaseRecordingCanvas.java)\\nBase class for deferred rendering canvases:\\n- Implements all Canvas draw operations as @FastNative calls\\n- Records commands instead of immediately rendering\\n- Used by both RecordingCanvas and potentially other recording implementations\\n- Avoids immediate GPU submission, batching for efficiency\\n\\n## Complete Rendering Flow:\\n\\n1. **Scheduling**: ViewRootImpl.scheduleTraversals() \u2192 Choreographer.postCallback(CALLBACK_TRAVERSAL)\\n2. **VSYNC Signal**: Choreographer receives VSYNC from DisplayEventReceiver (SurfaceFlinger)\\n3. **Traversal Execution**: Choreographer invokes doTraversal() \u2192 performTraversals()\\n4. **Measurement**: performMeasure() \u2192 View.measure() recursively for entire hierarchy\\n5. **Layout**: performLayout() \u2192 View.layout() recursively positioning all views\\n6. **Drawing**: performDraw() \u2192 initiates GPU rendering:\\n   - For each View: RenderNode.beginRecording() \u2192 RecordingCanvas\\n   - View.draw(RecordingCanvas) records operations\\n   - RenderNode.endRecording() finalizes display list\\n7. **GPU Rendering**: ThreadedRenderer queues display lists to render thread\\n8. **Frame Output**: Display list commands execute on GPU via HardwareRenderer\\n9. **Buffer Swap**: Surface buffer presents to display via SurfaceFlinger\\n\\nThis pipeline ensures smooth 60 FPS rendering synchronized with the display refresh rate through VSYNC timing.\"\n}\n",
